This recipe is delicious! I decided to bake instead of broil - 375 degrees for 30-40 minutes worked well.  I doubled the sauce recipe and it gave it a good amount of flavor. I also made cuts into the Salmon so that the sauce/ glaze could flavor the inside of the meat.  I served it with Jasmine rice & mixed vegetables and it was a delicious meal!

This was delicious.  I love salmon so I'm always looking for ways to prepare it.  This was simple to make and kept the flavor of the glaze.  We put it atop a lightly greased broiler pan (a little water on bottom pan to help steam it) and it baked for about 11 min's.  We also used a d.j. mustard with 'honey' in it which was a compliment to the brown sugar...Yum.

Thanks Tamara for a great recipe!

This is a surprisingly tasty recipe, given how few ingredients there are in it. We had it for dinner tonight and it is quick to make, and delicious. Next time, I am going to add some garlic, just for an extra zing. Thanks for sharing Tamara.

text:
Yum! I added a squeeze or two of honey to this, used about 1/2 tsp mustard powder, a squirt of yellow mustard (since that's all I had) and I added a little bit of minced garlic and a "tinse" of lemon juice. Cut some slits in the fish to let the glaze run through, and put a layer of tin foil on the bottom of the pan. Marinated about 10-15 minutes. Really tasty! Next time, I'll try substituting some honey instead of the brown sugar instead of adding it, since it made the sauce a bit too sweet. Thanks!

This is my new favorite way to eat salmon!  The easiest recipe EVER, and the flavor is so multi-dimensional!  I doubled the sauce and that was probably too much, but better that way than too little. text:
Super easy & amazing taste.  I followed original recipe without changes.  My 4 year old kept asking for more!  

A few tips:
  
(1) If broiling, set the rack in second from the top level because the broiling pan will give it extra height and you don't want to burn the glaze.  It took about 10 minutes to cook.  I poured a little water in the broiling pan and just used Pam to spray the grill, no need for aluminum foil.  Broil on LOW.
  
(2)  I made this recipe for 3 average size fillets and coated most of the top with glaze.  Although delicious, I think mine could have used more glaze coated thoroughly and perhaps letting it fall into the sides of fillet.  So for me, it wouldn't be enough glaze for 4 servings, just make more.

Great recipe, thanks!!!

text:
This was absolutely delicious! I had never really cooked fish before so I was a bit nervous I would mess something up but it was perfect! And very easy, particularly for a beginner like me. I followed some of the previous reviews and baked it at 400 degrees for about 20 minutes. I used a clear 13x9 baking pan and laid down foil first. When my husband and I went to lift it out of the pan, the skin came right off (and onto the tin foil, thank goodness)! I got two fresh, rather large filets from the Publix seafood counter - one side still had the skin and I cooked it skin-side down, no problems. I also put about a 1/4 cup of water into the pan with the fish. This will certainly be a repeated go-to in the future! (Oh! I also used dijon mustard with honey.)

text:
This recipe was sooo good yet super easy too! I seasoned my salmon with garlic salt, pepper, and smoked paprika. I got more creative with the glaze though. I used mostly dark brown sugar but also added about a tablespoon each of honey and organic agave nectar. (We like it sweet in my house! ) I also did not have any Dijon mustard in hand so i just used plain old yellow mustard. At the suggestion of another user, i cut a few slits into the salmon to let the glaze get into it more. I cooked the fish 24 mins in a foil lined dish and covered with foil as well. I broiled it on low for an additional 3 minutes. Super fast and delicious meal. My favorite comment on dinner: "I've never had fish like this. It's amazing! " Thanks for a great recipe. Definitely going into regular rotation!

Quite delicious. Wild caught salmon is preferred but, farm raised will even take to this glaze very well.

Don't skimp on the pepper, use fresh ground, even found in the Dollar Store, it helps to accent the tart of the mustard and offset the sweetness of the sugar.

Don't overcook your salmon - better rare then well done...

text:
Love it!  I made this super simple recipe, but I made a slight change to the cooking method.  I wrapped my broiler pan with tin foil, started the fish on the grill to give it a smokey flavor, then moved it inside to the broiler to finish it up.  (And keep an eye on it!)  The best part of the fish was the crispy thin super glaze.  I thought I had overcooked it, but it was excellent!  The thin part of the fish was sweeter, the thicker part of the fish was savory.   Served it on yellow rice and green beans.  I would DOUBLE the sauce for 4 fillets!

text:
OH MY!!  I made this recipe last night.  Unbelievably good. I will definitely make this recipe at least twice a month. Has plenty of possibilities by changing the dry spices.  And, since my husband and I like more savory than sweet dishes, I reduced the sugar to 1 Tbs. packed brown sugar and added 1/2 tsp. garlic powder and 1/4 tsp. onion powder, 1/2 tsp. black pepper and 1/4 tsp. sea salt to the mixture.  I then stirred everything  in a small bowl and basted the salmon steaks (two, each about 6 oz.) on all sides, placed on a rack inside a small baking dish and broiled for 15 minutes.  I did reserve about a tablespoon of the basting mixture for serving.  A definite keeper.  Thank you Tamara.

After reading reviews I was concerned about the sweetness of this recipe, after all, never heard of sugar and fish. This recipe is fantastic! It definitely has some sweetness that cuts the fishy taste of salmon but is hardly too sweet in my book. The fish broiled at 550 for about 10 mins and was cooked perfectly although my filet was only 2 thick. The only downside to this is the skin doesnt have a chance to crisp but the flesh comes clean of the skin with no effort so easy to eat around. Very surprised at the simplicity and that sugar and fish go together.

city:

country:

text:
YUM! This recipe was awesome and so easy to make! I looked at the reviews before I made it (something I always like to do to get a consensus about the recipe) and I did use some of the suggestions others had! I doubled the glaze recipe &  added 1 TBSP of honey and 1 TBSP soy sauce to my glaze. I also cut small holes into tops of salmon fillets before I salt & pepper, then coated mix on top and let marinate in fridge for about 1-2hours. I then put fillet on aluminum lined baking sheet then poured mix from container on top again. I baked them @ 350 degrees for 40 mind (check after 30 to make sure you dont over cook!) The glaze did burn on the foil but the salmon was lovely; very moist & juicy without drying out and glaze was thick enough. They turned out DELICIOUS! We were all fighting over the last piece and this is one meal that I know we will eat the leftovers haha. Thanks to OP for this recipe & I will be keeping it in my book for next time :)

text:
Don't think about it! Just do it! Simple, easy and wonderfully delicious! I added a teaspoon of soy sauce to mine and used organic light brown sugar and placedsalmon on aluminum foil before broiling on low for approx 15 - 18 minutes. I did put a few drops of water at the bottom and coconut oil just to make sure the moisture remained (you can spray the pan with cooking spray instead). The recipe is great just as is. You don't have to add anything to it. I served the salmon with brown rice and stir fry vegetables (carrots, peas, broccoli) and made some extra sauce to cover  lightly over the vegetables. You won't regret this. The kids are asking, is the food done already?!?!? The answer is...YES!

text:
This truly was an outstanding, easy, quick main dish.  The broiler needs to be on high.  I do not have a broiler pan, so I used my cookie sheet covered with aluminum foil and a cooling rack placed on top.  The salmon then sits on the cooling rack and the drippings land on the aluminum foil and not the cookie sheet.....super easy clean up.  I did let the salmon marinade for a couple hours.  I also substituted soy sauce for the salt.  Excellent!

Loved this recipe! I followed the recipe's exact instructions even with the 6 inches away from broiler fire instruction. My husband doesn't like sweet food but he did say it tasted like it came out of a restaurant. The only think I will add is that if you have a broiler like mine that only has a "Hi" and "Lo" setting, broil on "Hi" for 5 mins and "lo" for the next five. You get that golden brown look but not burnt taste.
